
►<field>pub.n="incomplete"</field><?phoenix upid="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883"?>
►<field>ch.rh="Judgments"</field>Chapter 10. Judgments
10:1. Scope
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|1|10:1"</field>This chapter contains forms for final judgments, some forms of orders that are final and some forms of orders that are not final, but partake more of judgments than of the usual interlocutory orders. This chapter also includes forms for final process and for enforcing final judgments.
10:2. Form and procedure
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|2|10:2"</field>Judgments and final orders, as well as the orders in this chapter that are not final, contain a caption in the form of the action, a designation as the appropriate judgment or order, a commencement that sometimes includes findings of fact and a body that contains the adjudications made by the judgment or order. See ►<field>x.ref.id="I05NKP4"</field>&s;§2:2; ►<field>st.ref.id="I03XWRW"</field>Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.100(c); ►<field>st.ref.id="I015V9P"</field>Fla. Fam. L. R. P. 12.100(c). Judgments and orders are completed by a conclusion that gives the date and place of entry and the signature of the judge. A notation of the parties or attorneys to whom conformed copies of the judgment have been sent is in the lower left-hand part of the form.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|2|10:2"</field>After a judgment is entered, it must be filed with the clerk, and recorded. If it is not a final judgment or order, it may be recorded if the court so orders. Interlocutory orders that deal with the title to or possession of real property should always be recorded.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|2|10:2"</field>The commencement of final judgments differs. There is one form for an application for judgment after default, others for judgment after motion for judgment on the pleadings, for summary judgment, for dismissal and for jury trials and nonjury trials. The commencement should recite the predicate for its entry, such as one of the motions, a jury or nonjury trial, and then move on to the adjudicatory paragraphs. Most lawyers call the judgment after a motion for summary judgment a summary judgment. It is not. It is a final judgment granted after a motion for summary judgment. It can properly be called a summary final judgment, but it is better to call it simply a final judgment.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|2|10:2"</field>The commencement must contain findings of fact in some cases.<trace> </trace><trace>►</trace><trace>The failure to include the required findings of fact in </trace><trace>a</trace><trace> final judgment</trace><trace> leave the judgment open to attack by rehearing, appeal, and ultimately a new trial</trace><trace>. </trace><trace>►</trace><trace>See Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.530</trace><trace> and Fam. L. R. P. 12.530.</trace>
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|2|10:2"</field>►<field>st.ref.id="I02T6UB"</field>Rule 1.560(c) of the Florida Rules of Civil Procedure was amended to authorize a requirement that a judgment debtor furnish a fact information sheet to the judgment creditor's attorney. See ►<field>st.ref.id="I05VWWO"</field>Fla. R. Civ. P. Form 1.977. The form may be subject to challenge in requiring a nonparty spouse to divulge separate property. A similar requirement form is authorized for small claims. See ►<field>st.ref.id="I052Z2G"</field>Fla. Sm. Cl. R. 7.221. The provision for the requirement is in ►<field>x.ref.id="I04693R"</field>&s;§10:13. It can be added to any other form to which it is applicable.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|2|10:2"</field>Costs are included in all of the forms of final judgments. Many times court costs cannot be awarded when judgment is entered so a motion to tax costs must be filed and a separate order taxing costs entered. See ►<field>x.ref.id="I01QR8R"</field>&s;§7:<trace>200</trace><trace.deleted/>&s;<trace.deleted/>; ►<field>x.ref.id="I046954"</field>&s;§7:201; ►<field>x.ref.id="I0469AR"</field>&s;§7:30<trace>5</trace><trace.deleted/>.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|2|10:2"</field>For a money judgment to become a lien on the judgment debtor's property it must contain the prevailing party's address and the non-prevailing party's address and Social Security number if known or an affidavit must be recorded with the information at the same time as the certified copy of the judgment.

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|2|10:2"</field>See ►<field>st.ref.id="I02T71J"</field>&s;§28.222(3)(c), Fla. Stat.; ►<field>st.ref.id="I02T776"</field>&s;§28.29, Fla. Stat. See ►<field>cc.ref.id="I05QEGP"</field>Sun Bank/Southwest, N.A. v. Schad, 482 So. 2d 554 (Fla. 2d DCA 1986) for the immediate issuance of the execution; and ►<field>cc.ref.id="I05NLHH"</field>Robinson v. Sterling Door & Window Co., Inc., 698 So. 2d 570 (Fla. 1st DCA 1997) for the requirement of the parties' addresses and the judgment debtor's party's Social Security number for money judgments. See ►<field>st.ref.id="I05VWI9"</field>&s;§55.10(2), Fla. Stat.

FINAL JUDGMENT 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|3|10:3"</field>This action was heard on the report of the special master and the exceptions to it and
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|3|10:3"</field>IT IS ADJUDGED that:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>1. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|3|10:3"</field>The special master's report is approved, except for the allowance of defendant's expense for attorney fees of $[dollar amount of attorney's fees] that is disallowed.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>2. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|3|10:3"</field>With the disallowance the report shows defendant owes plaintiff the sum of $[dollar amount of debt] and an accounting of the net proceeds from the sale of the remaining assets of the joint venture.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>3. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|3|10:3"</field>Defendant shall account to plaintiff for plaintiff's share of the net proceeds of the sale of the remaining assets of the joint venture:
►<field>fac.lo="n"</field>[specification of list of assets]
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|3|10:3"</field><field>p.fl="none"</field>within ten days after the sale of each asset.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>4. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|3|10:3"</field>Plaintiff [NAME OF PLAINTIFF], whose address is [address of plaintiff], recover from defendant [NAME OF DEFENDANT] [OPTIONAL:, whose address is [address of defendant] and the last four digits of Social Security number are [last four numbers of Social Security number],] the sum of $[dollar amount of judgment] with interest of $[dollar amount of interests] to the date of this judgment, and costs in the sum of $[dollar amount of costs], making a total of $[total dollar amount of costs], with interest at the rate prescribed by law, for which let execution issue forthwith.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|3|10:3"</field>ORDERED at [name of city], Florida on [date of order].

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|3|10:3"</field>This is the final judgment in a joint venture accounting after a reference. See ►<field>x.ref.id="I013B4T"</field>section 10:64 for the order determining the liability to account. This form assumes the attorney fee disallowance is for an improper charge and the balance of the accounting is proper. If the accounting shows no debt due plaintiff, paragraph 4 would be changed to the usual judgment for defendant. See ►<field>x.ref.id="I05OQKL"</field>&s;§10:12. This form can be used in family actions: See ►<field>x.ref.id="I05RJPH"</field>&s;§5:5, Comment.

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|4|10:4"</field>This action was heard on the petition for adoption<trace>. The petitioners and the minor child appeared before</trace><trace> the court. The</trace><trace.deleted/> court finds that <trace>a valid</trace><trace.deleted/> termination of parental rights has been adjudged<trace> and the date for a birth parent to file an appeal </trace><trace>of that judgment </trace><trace>has </trace><trace>pas</trace><trace>sed</trace>, <trace>a proper </trace><trace>home</trace><trace> study </trace>has <trace>been filed and </trace>reviewed<trace.deleted/><trace>,</trace> and <trace.deleted/>the best interests of the minor will be accomplished by the adoption so
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|4|10:4"</field>IT IS ADJUDGED that:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>1. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|4|10:4"</field>The [male/female] minor child born in [name of county], [name of state] on [date of birth] is the legal child of petitioners [names of petitioners] and shall be known as [new name of child] hereafter.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>2. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|4|10:4"</field>All legal relationships between the child and the child's former relatives<trace> have previously been </trace><trace.deleted/>terminated, including grandparental visitation, and the relationship of parents and child is created between the minor child and petitioners.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>3. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|4|10:4"</field>The name of the minor child is changed to [new name of child].
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|4|10:4"</field>ORDERED at [name of city], Florida on [date of order].

AMENDED FINAL JUDGMENT 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|5|10:5"</field>This action was heard on defendant's motion for rehearing and
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|5|10:5"</field>IT IS ADJUDGED that:

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|7|10:7"</field>This form was derived from ►<field>cc.ref.id="I02Z37H"</field>Musselwhite v. Oleson, 53 So. 944 (Fla. 1910). Rescission and cancellation are similar, but distinguishable because rescission effects a judicial voiding of the instrument. Cancellation requires the physical surrender of the instrument in order to effect the voiding. See ►<field>cc.ref.id="I02Z38M"</field>Willis v. Fowler, 136 So. 358 (Fla. 1931). Thus a recorded instrument can be rescinded, but it cannot be canceled since it is a part of the public records.

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|8|10:8"</field>This action seeks a writ of certiorari to the City of [name of city] to rezone the property described in the petition to permit construction of a commercial establishment. The property is presently zoned for single family residences only. The City refused to rezone the property at a public hearing. Petitioner contends that the City refused the rezoning petition because of the political pressure brought by the number of opponents of the rezoning request who were present at the public hearing. Petitioner did not have a court reporter present and the record from the electronic recording machines is so poor that the events transpiring at the hearing cannot be determined with certainty. Since there is an inadequate record of the proceedings below from which it can be determined that the City erred as a matter of law.

FINAL JUDGMENT 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|9|10:9"</field>This action seeks a writ of certiorari to the County Court of [name of county], Florida, to review a discovery order. Petitioner in this action is plaintiff in the county court and seeks damages for breach of contract. Defendant counterclaimed for malicious interference. Defendant propounded interrogatories seeking information about plaintiff's assets, liabilities, customer names and other financial information. The pleadings do not seek punitive damages at this stage and no discovery has been conducted as contemplated by ►<field>st.ref.id="I05Q5XJ"</field>&s;§768.72 Florida Statutes as a predicate for amending to plead punitive damages.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|9|10:9"</field>Plaintiff objected to interrogatories [designation of interrogatories] that seek financial and business information on the grounds that customers' names were a trade secret and financial information was not relevant. The county court overruled the objections and ordered plaintiff to provide the requested discovery.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|9|10:9"</field>Defendant supports the county court order on the grounds that it may lead to admissible evidence and provide the basis for punitive damages. Plaintiff contends that discovery on that basis is premature.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|9|10:9"</field>The court finds that the interrogatories are premature, except interrogatory 16 seeking customer names, so
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|9|10:9"</field>IT IS ADJUDGED that:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>1. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|9|10:9"</field>Certiorari is granted and the order of the County Court of [name of county], Florida dated [date of order] overruling plaintiff's objections to defendant's interrogatories is quashed, except for interrogatory [designation of interrogatory].
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>2. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|9|10:9"</field>This action is remanded to the County Court of [name of county], Florida for further proceedings consistent with this judgment.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>3. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|9|10:9"</field>Petitioner [NAME OF PLAINTIFF], whose address is [address of petitioner], recover from [NAME OF DEFENDANT] [OPTIONAL:, whose address is [address of defendant] and the last four digits of Social Security number are [last four numbers of Social Security number],] the sum of $[dollar amount of costs] for costs that shall bear interest at the rate prescribed by law, for which let execution issue forthwith.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|9|10:9"</field>ORDERED at [name of city], Florida on [date of order].

FINAL JUDGMENT 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>This action was tried before the court. On the evidence presented
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>IT IS ADJUDGED that:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>1. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>Defendant did not construct the apartment building as specified by the drawings and specifications in the following particulars:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(a). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>The concrete in the grade beams and columns was not of the strength specified, testing at less than half the required strength;
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(b). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>The interior drywall was exposed to the elements before installation with resulting deterioration so that it buckled and would not take wallpaper;
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(c). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>Aluminum electrical wiring was installed instead of copper.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>2. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>The completion of the building was delayed by 187 days. The contractor is responsible for 92 days of delay. The remaining delay was caused by the failure of the architect to prepare the drawings and specification in accordance with the Standard Building Code and to promptly process change orders.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>3. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>Plaintiff did not pay defendant at the times required by the contract documents. The delays in timely payments caused damages to defendant of $67,258.19 in lost discounts, interest on delayed payments and disruption of defendant's operations on the project.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>4. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>Defendant's delay in completion, disregarding the delays caused by the architect, caused plaintiff to lose $30,000 in rent.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>5. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>Change orders directed by plaintiff that have not been paid to defendant have a value of $110,516.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>6. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>The apartment building was not substantially completed because of the defects listed in paragraph 1. Nevertheless, plaintiff elected to accept the building and sought an equitable reduction in the contract price. Plaintiff is entitled to a reduction of $180,500 for the defects.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>7. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>Defendant's surety is jointly and severally liable with defendant to plaintiff under the performance bond for the failure to perform the contract. The surety is not liable under the payment bond for reimbursement to plaintiff for amounts paid to discharge construction liens because the bond contains a condition precedent that plaintiff pay progress payments in accordance with the contract documents. Plaintiff did not do so as adjudged in paragraph 3.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>8. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>Defendant and the surety are liable to plaintiff for $32,725.81.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>9. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>Jurisdiction is reserved to award supplemental relief and attorney fees and to tax costs.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>ORDERED at [name of city], Florida on [date of order].

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|14|10:14"</field>A judgment for declaratory relief must give the requested declaration. See ►<field>cc.ref.id="I04829L"</field>Ennis v. Warm Mineral Springs, Inc., 203 So. 2d 514 (Fla. 2d DCA 1967); ►<field>cc.ref.id="I04594P"</field>Hildebrandt v. Department of Natural Resources, Division of Interior Resources, 313 So. 2d 73 (Fla. 3d DCA 1975). This applies even when the declaration is against the plaintiff. Paragraph 8 of the form is an adjudication of liability. It is not a judgment for money. This form assumes the pleadings did not contain a predicate for the money judgment. The money judgment can be obtained by a motion for supplemental relief.

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|15|10:15"</field>See ►<field>st.ref.id="I04BQJR"</field>Fla. R. Civ. P. Form 1.988(b). The address and Social Security number of the defendant are omitted because most often they are not known. If known, the address and last four digits of the Social Security number must be inserted. See ►<field>x.ref.id="I05RJPN"</field>&s;§10:13, Comment.<trace> . If the Plaintiff owes the attorney for the services rendered, consideration should be given to including language that payment is to be made directly to the lawyer and failure of the defendant to pay said funds shall also be actionable by the lawyer.</trace>

10:16. Judgment-- Default, damages, no prejudgment interest or attorney fees

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|16|10:16"</field>See ►<field>st.ref.id="I04BQJO"</field>Fla. R. Civ. P. Form 1.988<trace> </trace>(a); ►<field>x.ref.id="I02KOFP"</field>&s;§10:13, Comment; ►<field>x.ref.id="I02T7SO"</field>&s;§10:15, Comment. The address and the last four digits of the Social Security number for the defendant are omitted because generally when default occurs these are not known to the plaintiff.

►<field>fac.lo="n"</field>FINAL JUDGMENT DISSOLVING CORPORATION
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|22|10:22"</field>This action was tried before the court. On the evidence presented the court finds that the directors of [NAME OF DEFENDANT CORPORATION] are deadlocked in the management of the corporate affairs and the shareholders are unable to break the deadlock. As a result irreparable injury to the corporate defendant's assets is now being suffered and unless the action taken under this final judgment occurs, the assets will be lost to the shareholders. The corporation has complied with ►<field>st.ref.id="I04BHVZ"</field>&s;§607.1431(4), Fla. Stat., however the shareholders have not elected to purchase the plaintiff's shares, therefore
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|22|10:22"</field>IT IS ADJUDGED that:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>1. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|22|10:22"</field>Defendant [NAME OF DEFENDANT CORPORATION] is dissolved effective [date of dissolution].
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>2. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|22|10:22"</field>The directors shall sell all of the assets of the corporation as soon as possible. When sufficient assets are sold so that all creditors can be paid, the directors of the corporation shall pay the debts of the corporation.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>3. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|22|10:22"</field>If there is an excess of funds after the debts of the corporation are paid, the balance after paying the debts of the corporation shall be paid to the stockholders of the corporation pro rata according to the amounts of stock owned by each.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>4. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|22|10:22"</field>The directors of the corporation shall follow the procedures prescribed by &ss;§§607.1406 and 607.1407, Florida Statutes as may be necessary to dispose of all claims against the corporation by its creditors.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>5. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|22|10:22"</field>The court reserves jurisdiction of the corporation to enforce this judgment and to enter any other orders that may be necessary for the complete and proper disposition of the corporation's assets.

On the evidence presented the court finds that plaintiff's attorney has reasonably expended [number of hours] hours in representing plaintiff in this action and that $[dollar hourly rate of attorney's fees] is a reasonable hourly rate for the services and that defendant [NAME OF LIENOR] attorney has reasonably expended [number of hours] hours in the representation of defendant in this action and that $[dollar amount of hourly rate of attorney's fees] is a reasonable hourly rate for the services, so
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|32|10:32"</field>IT IS ADJUDGED that:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>1. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|32|10:32"</field>Plaintiff [NAME OF PLAINTIFF], whose address is [address of plaintiff], is due $[dollar amount of improvements] for labor, services and material furnished to improve the real property described in paragraph 2, $[dollar amount of interest] as interest to the date of this judgment, $[dollar amount of attorney's fees] for attorney fees with costs of $[dollar amount of costs], making a total of $[total dollar amount of judgment] that shall bear interest at the rate of [rate of interest]&percnt;% a year.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>2. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|32|10:32"</field>Plaintiff holds a construction lien for the total sum superior to any claim or interest of defendant [NAME OF DEFENDANT OWNER] on the following real property in [name of county], Florida:
►<field>fac.lo="n"</field>[description of property].
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>3. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|32|10:32"</field>If the total sum with interest at the rate prescribed in paragraph 1 and all costs of this action accruing subsequent to this judgment are not paid, the clerk of this court shall sell the property at public sale on [date of sale], between 11:00 a.m. and 2:00 p.m., to the highest bidder for cash, except as prescribed in paragraphs 4 and 5, at the [location of sale] door of the courthouse in [name of county] in accordance with ►<field>st.ref.id="I03HNW1"</field>&s;§45.031, Fla. Stat. The clerk of this court shall receive the service charge pursuant to ►<field>st.ref.id="I03HNUW"</field>&s;§45.035, Fla. Stat. in making, recording, and certifying the sale and title that shall be assessed as costs.

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|32|10:32"</field>Plaintiff shall advance all subsequent costs of this action and shall be reimbursed for them by the clerk if plaintiff is not the purchaser of the property at the sale. If plaintiff is the purchaser, the clerk shall credit plaintiff's bid with the prorated amount specified in paragraph 6, not to exceed the total sum due plaintiff, with interest and costs accruing subsequent to this judgment, or such part of it, as is necessary to fully pay the bid.

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|32|10:32"</field>After filing the certificate of title the clerk shall distribute the proceeds of the sale, so far as they are sufficient, by paying: first, all plaintiff's and defendant [NAME OF LIENOR] costs; second, documentary stamps affixed to the certificate; third, plaintiff's and defendant [NAME OF LIENOR] attorney fees; fourth, the total sum due to plaintiff and defendant less the items paid plus interest from this date to the date of the sale; and shall retain any remaining amount for subsequent distribution pursuant to ►<field>st.ref.id="I03HNP6"</field>&s;§45.031 Fla. FINAL JUDGMENT 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|46|10:46"</field>This action was tried before the court. On the evidence presented the court finds that plaintiff's attorney has reasonably expended [number of hours] hours in representing plaintiff and that $[dollar amount of services] is a reasonable hourly rate for the services, and defendant's attorney has reasonably expended [number of hours] hours in representing defendant and that $[dollar amount of services] is a reasonable hourly rate for the services, so
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|46|10:46"</field>IT IS ADJUDGED that:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>1. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|46|10:46"</field>Plaintiff [NAME OF PLAINTIFF], whose address is [address of plaintiff], and defendant [NAME OF DEFENDANT] each own an undivided [specification of fraction of interest] interest as tenants in common in the real property in [name of county], Florida described as:
►<field>fac.lo="n"</field>[legal description of property].
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>2. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|46|10:46"</field>The property is indivisible and cannot be partitioned in kind.
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>3. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|46|10:46"</field>The clerk of this court shall sell the property at public sale on [date of auction] between 11:00 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. to the highest bidder for cash, except as provided in paragraph 5, at the [location of sale] door of the courthouse in [name of county] in [name of town], Florida in accordance with ►<field>st.ref.id="I05XUEN"</field>&s;§45.031 Florida Statutes. Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|48|10:48"</field>See ►<field>cc.ref.id="I03TKZT"</field>State ex rel. Ervin v. Smith, 160 So. 2d 518 (Fla. 1964). When judgment is for defendant, the action is dismissed. See ►<field>x.ref.id="I03UP3C"</field>&s;§10:18. The commencement in this action omits the reference to the presentation of evidence even though it is a nonjury form. This is so because an issue of fact in prohibition is virtually impossible. See ►<field>x.ref.id="I03XI88"</field>&s;§10:73 (for the writ). This is a review action so the appellate rules govern. See ►<field>st.ref.id="I0359XP"</field>Fla. R. App. P. 9.100(f).

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|49|10:49"</field>This example was derived from ►<field>cc.ref.id="I06ZD3E"</field>Rabinowitz v. Keefer, 132 So. 297 (Fla. 1931) omitting the findings and incorporating the reason for the action in paragraph 2. No provision for costs is made because it is usually futile. If a defendant is alive and subject to personal jurisdiction, a paragraph assessing costs should be added. In the rare case of a contested quiet title action, the form would follow the commencement in ►<field>x.ref.id="I013K10"</field>section 10:50 and add a paragraph on costs.

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|58|10:58"</field>This example was dervied from ►<field>cc.ref.id="I0308HO"</field>Carter v. Colson, 194 So. 619 (Fla. 1940) and ►<field>cc.ref.id="I0308IT"</field>Musselwhite v. Oleson, 60 Fla. 342, 53 So. 944 (Fla. 1910). Rescission and cancellation are similar, but distinguishable because rescission effects a judicial voiding of the instrument. Cancellation requires the physical surrender of the instrument in order to effect the voiding of it. See ►<field>cc.ref.id="I0308IW"</field>Willis v. Fowler, 136 So. 358 (Fla. 1931).

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|63|10:63"</field>This action was tried before the court on all issues, except compensation for the way of necessity. Pursuant to the verdict rendered in this action on compensation, the court hereinafter adjudicates the amount of compensation for the way of necessity. On the evidence presented

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|63|10:63"</field>The way of necessity shall be over the following described property of defendant [NAME OF DEFENDANT] in [name of county], Florida:

 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|64|10:64"</field>Accountings have two phases. The first phase is on the liability to account. This form is a determination of liability. CONTINUING WRIT OF GARNISHMENT 
 ►<field>fal.lo="n"</field>THE STATE OF FLORIDA:
 ►<field>fal.lo="n"</field>To Each Sheriff of the State:
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>YOU ARE COMMANDED to summon garnishee [NAME OF GARNISHEE] to serve an answer to this writ on [name of plaintiff's attorney], plaintiff's attorney, whose address is [address of plaintiff's attorney], and to file the original with the clerk of this court either before service on the attorney or immediately thereafter, stating:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>1. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>whether defendant [NAME OF DEFENDANT]is employed by garnishee, and
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>2. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>if so, the gross amount of periodic payments of salary or wages payable to defendant, and
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>3. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>the pay period for defendant, and requiring garnishee to withhold from each payment due or coming due of defendant's salary or wages after the service of this writ the amount exceeding:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(a). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>[text dollar amount of weekly amount] dollar if defendant is paid weekly;
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(b). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>[text dollar amount of bi-weekly amount] dollar if defendant is paid bi-weekly;
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(c). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>[text dollar amount of semi-monthly amount] dollar if defendant is paid semi-monthly; or
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(d). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>[text dollar amount of monthly amount] dollar if defendant is paid monthly; and
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(e). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>in addition to the above amount withheld, garnishee may retain up to $[dollar amount of retention] for the first deduction and $[dollar amount of subsequent retentions] for each subsequent deduction for administrative expenses.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>BUT IN NO EVENT to withhold more than 25&percnt;% of the gross salary or wages of defendant after deducting Social Security and income withholding taxes. If defendant is the head of a family residing in Florida, no amount shall be withheld unless the defendant has signed a statutory waiver and earns more than $750 a week. The head of a family is a person who is providing more than one-half of the support for a child or other dependent. If defendant claims to be the head of a family, garnishee shall notify defendant to seek an exemption from this writ and to consult an attorney about the exemption.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>Otherwise, withholding shall continue until plaintiff's judgment in the sum of $[dollar amount of judgment] is satisfied or defendant's employment by garnishee terminates or the further order of this court. Withheld payments shall be retained by garnishee until the further order of this court.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>A failure to comply with this writ may result in garnishee paying the garnished amounts twice and in garnishee being held in contempt of court.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>ORDERED at [name of city], Florida on [date of garnishment].

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|69|10:69"</field>See ►<field>st.ref.id="I048WNM"</field>&s;§77.0305, Fla. Stat. This example was derived from ►<field>st.ref.id="I02UL6A"</field>Florida Rule of Civil Procedure Form 1.907<trace> </trace>(b). See ►<field>x.ref.id="I05QEU4"</field>&s;§10:66 for the order to issue the writ. This form contains the method of computing the amounts to be withheld in accordance with the ►<field>sst.ref.id="I05XU9I"</field>Consumer Credit Protection Act, ►<field>st.ref.id="I05V14M"</field>Title 15 U.S.C.A. &s;§1673(b). It is based on the minimum wage effective September 1, 1997. It limits the computation of disposable earnings and the deductions of Social Security and withholding taxes. Federal cases do not permit the exclusion of other items although many forms of Florida writs do so. See ►<field>cc.ref.id="I03W4UL"</field>First Nat. Bank v. Hasty, 415 F. Supp. 170 (E.D. Mich. 1976), aff'd, 573 F.2d 1310 (6th Cir. 1977) and aff'd, 573 F.2d 1310 (6th Cir. 1977). The form in this section is not for a writ connected with child support or alimony. The form for child support or alimony is in ►<field>x.ref.id="I044K99"</field>&s;§10:70. The form includes the exemption provided in ►<field>st.ref.id="I02XEB8"</field>section 222.11, Florida Statutes for the head of a family that most writs do not.

CONTINUING WRIT OF GARNISHMENT 
 ►<field>fal.lo="n"</field>THE STATE OF FLORIDA:
 ►<field>fal.lo="n"</field>To Each Sheriff of the State:
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>YOU ARE COMMANDED to summon garnishee [NAME OF GARNISHEE] to serve an answer to this writ on [name of petitioner's attorney], petitioner's attorney, whose address is [address of petitioner's attorney], within 20 days after service of this writ, exclusive of the day of service, and to file the original with the clerk of this court either before service on the attorney or immediately thereafter, stating:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>1. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>whether respondent [NAME OF RESPONDENT] is employed by garnishee, and
►<field>fi.lvl="1"</field>2. 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>if so, the amount of periodic payments of salary or wages payable to respondent,
and requiring garnishee to withhold from each payment due or coming due of respondent's salary or wages after the service of this writ the amount exceeding:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(a). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>$[dollar amount of weekly amount] if respondent is paid weekly;
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(b). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>$[dollar amount of bi-weekly amount] if respondent is paid bi-weekly;
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(c). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>$[dollar amount of semi-monthly amount] if respondent is paid semi-monthly; or
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(d). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>$[dollar amount of monthly amount] if respondent is paid monthly; and
►<field>fi.lvl="2"</field>(e). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>in addition to the above amounts withheld, garnishee may retain up to $[dollar amount of retention] for the first deduction and $[dollar amount of subsequent retentions] for each subsequent deduction for administrative expenses.
BUT IN NO EVENT to withhold more than the following percentages of the gross salary or wages of respondent after deducting Social Security and income withholding taxes:
 
►<field>fi.lvl="3"</field>(1). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>50&percnt;% if respondent is supporting a wife or dependent child other than the ones for whose benefit this writ is issued;
►<field>fi.lvl="3"</field>(2). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>60&percnt;% otherwise;
►<field>fi.lvl="3"</field>(3). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>55&percnt;% if respondent is supporting a spouse or dependent child other than the ones for whose benefit this writ is issued and if the amounts due are accrued 12 weeks or more before the payment being withheld; or
►<field>fi.lvl="3"</field>(4). 
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>65&percnt;% otherwise and the amount due accrued 12 weeks or more before the payment from which withholding is to be made.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>Withholding shall continue until the total amount of $[dollar amount of judgment] is satisfied or defendant's employment by garnishee terminates or the further order of this court. Withheld payments shall be retained by garnishee until the further order of this court, but if garnishee is deducting payments under any prior income deduction order or continuing garnishment for alimony or child support, application must be made to this court to determine the amounts to be withheld and their allocation.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>A failure to comply with this writ may result in garnishee paying the garnished amounts twice and garnishee being held in contempt of court.
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>ORDERED at [name of city], Florida on [date of garnishment].

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|70|10:70"</field>See ►<field>st.ref.id="I01VMC0"</field>&s;§61.12, Flat. Stat.; &s;§77.0305, Fla. Stat. The method of computing the exemption under the ►<field>sst.ref.id="I044SL6"</field>Consumer Credit Protection Act, ►<field>st.ref.id="I047LQ2"</field>Title 15 U.S.C.A. &s;§1673(b), is shown in ►<field>x.ref.id="I013KM8"</field>section 10:69. The sums in subparagraphs (a)&ndash;-(d) are based on the federal minimum wage effective September 1, 1997. The only difference between the two writs is the maximum amount that can be withheld and in containing no exemptions. This form has been largely supplanted by the income deduction order in ►<field>x.ref.id="I05T808"</field>&s;§10:65. See ►<field>st.ref.id="I048WMA"</field>&s;§61.1301(1), Fla. Stat.

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|73|10:73"</field>This example was derived from ►<field>cc.ref.id="I0308VR"</field>State ex rel. Ayala v. Knott, 3 So. 2d 522 (Fla. 1941). The form in the cited case is for an alternative writ. This form has been modified to make it perpetual or absolute. This is a review action so Florida Rule of Appellate Procedure 9.100(f) governs.
10:74. Judgment-- Satisfactions

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|74|10:74"</field>See ►<field>st.ref.id="I048OIV"</field>Fla. R. Civ. P. Form 1.981. The form must be changed to accommodate the change from Official Records Books in those counties that do not use that terminology.
10:75. Final disposition form

Author's Comment
 ►<field>p.ct.id="3d29be30775711ee8e1ba9ecff0bf883|75|10:75"</field>See ►<field>st.ref.id="I048OIS"</field>Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.545. The Supreme Court adopted <trace>►</trace>Form 1.998 in civil procedure and <trace>►</trace>Form 12.999 in family procedure. The appropriate form must be filed by the plaintiff or petitioner in family actions and by the prevailing party in civil actions when the matter is finally disposed of. The clerk files it for a pro se party or when the action is dismissed for lack of prosecution.
